A diagram of the [Battle of Baltim](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Baltim "Battle of Baltim")

On the first day of the war, Egyptian [missile boats](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missile_boat "Missile boat") bombarded Israeli positions on the Sinai coast; targeting Rumana, Ras Beyron, Ras Masala and Ras Sudar on the Mediterranean and Sharm el-Sheikh on the Red Sea coast of the Sinai Peninsula. Egyptian [frogmen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frogman "Frogman") raided the oil installations at Bala'eem, disabling the massive driller.[[326]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHammad2002100%E2%80%93101-331) Several small naval engagements took place on 7 October, including the [Battle of Latakia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Latakia "Battle of Latakia") and [Battle of Marsa Talamat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Marsa_Talamat "Battle of Marsa Talamat").[[327]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-332)

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:StiksSyrianShore10101973.jpg)

A Syrian Styx missile fired at an Israeli missile boat

The [Battle of Baltim](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Baltim "Battle of Baltim"), which took place on 8–9 October off the coast of [Baltim](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltim "Baltim") and [Damietta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damietta "Damietta"), ended in a decisive Israeli victory. Six Israeli missile boats heading towards Port Said encountered four Egyptian missile boats coming from [Alexandria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandria "Alexandria"). In an engagement lasting about forty minutes, the Israelis evaded Egyptian [Styx missiles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/P-15_Termit "P-15 Termit") using electronic countermeasures and sank three of the Egyptian missile boats with [Gabriel missiles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_(missile) "Gabriel (missile)") and gunfire.[[328]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-dunstan114-333)[[329]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-bolia-334)[[330]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich1988256%E2%80%93262Dupuy1978562%E2%80%93563Herzog1982312-335) The Battles of Latakia and Baltim "drastically changed the operational situation at sea to Israeli advantage".[[331]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-336)

Five nights after the Battle of Baltim, five Israeli patrol boats entered the Egyptian anchorage at [Ras Ghareb](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ras_Ghareb "Ras Ghareb"), where over fifty Egyptian small patrol craft and armed fishing boats mobilized for the war effort and loaded with troops, ammunition, and supplies bound for the Israeli side of the Gulf were based. In the battle that followed, 19 Egyptian boats were sunk, while others remained bottled up in port.[[217]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-almog-221)

The Israeli Navy had control of the Gulf of Suez during the war, which made possible the continued deployment of an Israeli SAM battery near an Israeli naval base close to the southern end of the Suez Canal, depriving the Egyptian Third Army of air support and preventing it from moving southward and attempting to capture the southern Sinai.[[332]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-337)

On 18 October, Israeli frogmen set off an explosion that severed two underwater communications cables off [Beirut](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beirut "Beirut"), one of which led to Alexandria and the other to [Marseille](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marseille "Marseille"). As a result, [telex](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telex "Telex") and telecommunications between the West and Syria were severed, and were not restored until the cables were repaired on 27 October. The cables had also been used by the Syrians and Egyptians to communicate with each other in preference to using radio, which was monitored by Israeli, U.S. and Soviet intelligence. Egypt and Syria resorted to communicating via a Jordanian radio station in [Ajloun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajloun "Ajloun"), bouncing the signals off a U.S. satellite.[[333]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-O'Ballance,_p._157-338)

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Baniasfmkesh.jpg)

A Syrian oil terminal in [Baniyas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baniyas "Baniyas") after being shelled by Israeli [Sa'ar 3-class missile boats](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sa%27ar_3-class_missile_boat "Sa'ar 3-class missile boat")

Having decisively beaten the Egyptian and Syrian navies, the Israeli Navy had the run of the coastlines. Israeli missile boats utilized their 76 mm cannons and other armaments to strike targets along the Egyptian and Syrian coastlines, including wharves, oil tank farms, coastal batteries, radar stations, airstrips, and other targets of military value. The Israeli Navy even attacked some of Egypt's northernmost SAM batteries.[[334]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-339)[[335]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-340) The Israeli Navy's attacks were carried out with minimal support from the IAF (only one Arab naval target was destroyed from the air during the entire war).[[217]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-almog-221)

The Egyptian Navy managed to enforce a blockade at [Bab-el-Mandeb](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb "Bab-el-Mandeb"). Eighteen million tons of oil had been transported yearly from [Iran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran") to Israel through the straits of Bab-el-Mandeb. The blockade was enforced by two Egyptian destroyers and two submarines, supported by ancillary craft. Shipping destined for Israel through the [Gulf of Eilat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Eilat "Gulf of Eilat") was halted by the Egyptians. The Israeli Navy had no means of lifting the blockade due to the long range involved, and the Israeli Air Force, apparently also incapable of lifting the blockade, did not challenge it. The blockade was lifted on 1 November, after Israel used the surrounded Egyptian Third Army as a bargaining chip. The Egyptians unsuccessfully attempted to blockade the Israeli Mediterranean coastline, and mined the Gulf of Suez to prevent the transportation of oil from the Bala'eem and Abu Rudeis oil fields in southwestern Sinai to [Eilat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eilat "Eilat") in southern Israel. Two oil tankers, of 48,000 ton and 2,000 ton capacity, sank after hitting mines in the Gulf.[[336]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-341)[[337]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003287-342)

According to Admiral [Ze'ev Almog](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ze%27ev_Almog "Ze'ev Almog"), the Israeli Navy escorted tankers from the Gulf to Eilat throughout the war, and Israeli tankers sailing from Iran were directed to bypass the Red Sea. As a result of these actions and the failure of Egypt's Mediterranean blockade, the transport of oil, grain and weapons to Israeli ports was made possible throughout nearly the entire war. A post-war survey found that during the entire war period, Israel suffered no oil shortages, and even sold oil to third parties affected by the Arab oil embargo.[[217]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-almog-221) This claim was disputed by [Edgar O'Ballance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_O%27Ballance "Edgar O'Ballance"), who claimed that no oil went to Israel during the blockade, and the Eilat-[Ashdod](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashdod "Ashdod") pipeline was empty by the end of the war.[[338]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Ballance1978326-343)

Israel responded with a counter-blockade of Egypt in the Gulf of Suez. The Israeli blockade was enforced by naval vessels based at Sharm el-Sheikh and on the Sinai coast facing the Gulf of Suez. The Israeli blockade substantially damaged the Egyptian economy. According to historian Gammal Hammad, Egypt's principal ports, Alexandria and [Port Safaga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_Safaga "Port Safaga"), remained open to shipping throughout the war.[[326]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHammad2002100%E2%80%93101-331) Throughout the war, the Israeli Navy enjoyed complete command of the seas both in the Mediterranean approaches and in the Gulf of Suez.[[339]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerzog1975268%E2%80%93269-344)

During the last week of the war, Egyptian frogmen carried out three or four raids on Eilat. The attacks caused minor damage, but created some alarm.[[333]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-O'Ballance,_p._157-338)

According to Israeli and Western sources, the Israelis lost no vessels in the war.[[328]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-dunstan114-333)[[329]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-bolia-334)[[340]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris2011432-345)[[341]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerzog1982314-346) Israeli vessels were "targeted by as many as 52 Soviet-made anti-ship missiles", but none hit their targets.[[342]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-347) According to historian [Benny Morris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Morris "Benny Morris"), the Egyptians lost seven missile boats and four torpedo boats and coastal defense craft, while the Syrians lost five missile boats, one minesweeper, and one coastal defense vessel.[[340]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris2011432-345)

### U.S.–Soviet naval standoff

The war saw the largest naval confrontation between the [United States Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy") and [Soviet Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Navy "Soviet Navy") of the entire Cold War. As the United States and Soviet Union supported their respective allies, their fleets in the Mediterranean became increasingly hostile toward each other. The Soviet [5th Operational Squadron](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/5th_Operational_Squadron "5th Operational Squadron") had 52 ships in the Mediterranean when the war began, including 11 submarines, some of which carried cruise missiles with nuclear warheads. The [United States Sixth Fleet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Sixth_Fleet "United States Sixth Fleet") had 48, including two aircraft carriers, a [helicopter carrier](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helicopter_carrier "Helicopter carrier"), and amphibious vessels carrying 2,000 marines.[[343]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-The_war_that_nearly_was-348)[[344]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-pri.org-349)

As the war continued, both sides reinforced their fleets. The Soviet squadron grew to 97 vessels including 23 submarines, while the US Sixth Fleet grew to 60 vessels including 9 submarines, 2 helicopter carriers, and 3 aircraft carriers. Both fleets made preparations for war, and US aircraft conducted reconnaissance over the Soviet fleet. The two fleets began to disengage following the ceasefire.[[343]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-The_war_that_nearly_was-348)[[344]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-pri.org-349)

Participation by other states
-----------------------------

### U.S. intelligence efforts

The U.S. intelligence community, including the CIA, failed to predict in advance the Egyptian–Syrian attack on Israel. A U.S. intelligence report as late as 4 October still stated that "We continue to believe that an outbreak of major Arab–Israeli hostilities remains unlikely for the immediate future".[[345]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-350) However, one U.S. government source that was able to predict the approaching war was Roger Merrick, an analyst working for the INR ([Bureau of Intelligence and Research](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureau_of_Intelligence_and_Research "Bureau of Intelligence and Research") in the State Department), but his conclusions were ignored at the time, and the report he had written to that effect was only rediscovered by U.S. government archive officials in 2013.[[346]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-351)

### U.S. aid to Israel

Main article: [Operation Nickel Grass](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Nickel_Grass "Operation Nickel Grass")

Based on intelligence estimates at the commencement of hostilities, American leaders expected the tide of the war to quickly shift in Israel's favor, and that Arab armies would be completely defeated within 72 to 96 hours.[[347]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-352) On 6 October, Secretary of State Kissinger convened the [National Security Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council "United States National Security Council")'s official crisis management group, the Washington Special Actions Group, which debated whether the U.S. should supply additional arms to Israel. High-ranking representatives of the [Defense](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense") and [State Departments](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State "United States Department of State") opposed such a move. Kissinger was the sole dissenter; he said that if the U.S. refused aid, Israel would have little incentive to conform to American views in postwar diplomacy. Kissinger argued the sending of U.S. aid might cause Israel to moderate its territorial claims, but this thesis raised a protracted debate whether U.S. aid was likely to make it more accommodating or more intransigent toward the Arab world.[[348]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-353)

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Israeli_M48_tank_captured_by_Egypt.jpg)

An Israeli [M48 Patton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/M48_Patton "M48 Patton") captured by Egyptian forces

By 8 October, Israel had encountered military difficulties on both fronts. In the Sinai, Israeli efforts to break through Egyptian lines with armor had been thwarted, and while Israel had contained and begun to turn back the Syrian advance, Syrian forces were still overlooking the [Jordan River](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_River "Jordan River") and their air defense systems were inflicting a high toll on Israeli planes.[[100]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuandt2005109-104)[[349]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-time19760412-354)[[350]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-farr-355) It became clear by 9 October that no quick reversal in Israel's favor would occur and that IDF losses were unexpectedly high.[[351]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Oct8AMconvo-356)

During the night of 8–9 October, an alarmed Dayan told Meir that "this is the end of the third temple."[[349]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-time19760412-354) He was warning of Israel's impending total defeat, but "Temple" was also the code word for [Israel's nuclear weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel "Nuclear weapons and Israel").[[350]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-farr-355) Dayan raised the nuclear topic in a cabinet meeting, warning that the country was approaching a point of "last resort".[[352]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-cohennyt-357) That night, Meir authorized the assembly of thirteen 20-kiloton-of-TNT (84 TJ) [tactical nuclear weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tactical_nuclear_weapon "Tactical nuclear weapon") for [Jericho missiles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jericho_(missile) "Jericho (missile)") at [Sdot Micha Airbase](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sdot_Micha_Airbase "Sdot Micha Airbase") and F-4 Phantom II aircraft at [Tel Nof Airbase](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Nof_Airbase "Tel Nof Airbase").[[350]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-farr-355) They would be used if absolutely necessary to prevent total defeat, but the preparation was done in an easily detectable way, likely as a signal to the United States.[[352]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-cohennyt-357) Kissinger learned of the nuclear alert on the morning of 9 October. That day, President Nixon ordered the commencement of [Operation Nickel Grass](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Nickel_Grass "Operation Nickel Grass"), an American [airlift](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airlift "Airlift") to replace all of Israel's material losses.[[49]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-GutfeldVanetik2016-53)

Anecdotal evidence suggests that Kissinger told Sadat that the reason for the U.S. airlift was that the Israelis were close to "going nuclear".[[350]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-farr-355) However, subsequent interviews with Kissinger, Schlesinger, and [William Quandt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Quandt "William Quandt") suggested that the nuclear aspect was not a major factor in the decision to re-supply. These officials cited the ongoing Soviet re-supply effort and Sadat's early rejection of a ceasefire as the primary motivators.[[353]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-358) European countries refused to allow U.S. airplanes carrying supplies for Israel to refuel at their bases, fearing an Arab oil embargo, with the exception of [Portugal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portugal "Portugal") and the [Netherlands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands"). Portugal permitted the United States to use the leased base of [Lajes Field](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lajes_Air_Base "Lajes Air Base") in the [Azores](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azores "Azores"),[[354]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-WhichChileAllende-359)[[355]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-ATaleOfTwoFleets-360)[[356]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-LeadershipLessonsFromHistoryLajesAirBase-361) and the defence minister of the Netherlands, apparently acting without consulting his cabinet colleagues, secretly authorised the use of Dutch airfields.[[357]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-NetherlandsHelp-362) Greece, then under the dictatorial rule of the [Regime of the Colonels](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_military_junta_of_1967%E2%80%931974 "Greek military junta of 1967–1974"), declared itself neutral in the conflict. However, the Greek junta permitted the United States to use communications facilities within Greece and the airports at Athens and at [Souda Naval Base](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Souda_Naval_Base "Souda Naval Base") to facilitate its assistance to Israel, though it refused to allow the Americans to use its strategically important bases in Cyprus.[[358]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-JohnSakkas2007-363)

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nickel_Grass_M60_C-5.jpg)

 An M60 delivered during [Operation Nickel Grass](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Nickel_Grass "Operation Nickel Grass")

Israel began receiving supplies via U.S. Air Force cargo airplanes on 14 October,[[359]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-364) although some equipment had arrived on planes from Israel's national airline [El Al](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Al "El Al") before this date. By that time, the IDF had advanced deep into Syria and was mounting a largely successful invasion of the Egyptian mainland from the Sinai, but had taken severe material losses. According to Abraham Rabinovich, "while the American airlift of supplies did not immediately replace Israel's losses in equipment, it did allow Israel to expend what it did have more freely".[[360]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004491-365)

By the end of Nickel Grass, the United States had shipped 22,395 tons of matériel to Israel. 8,755 tons of it arrived before the end of the war.[[361]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaberSchiff2003382-366) American [C-141 Starlifter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-141_Starlifter "C-141 Starlifter") and [C-5 Galaxy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-5_Galaxy "C-5 Galaxy") aircraft flew 567 missions throughout the airlift.[[362]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-367) El Al planes flew in an additional 5,500 tons of matériel in 170 flights.[[363]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003275%E2%80%93276-368)[[364]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaberSchiff2003282-369) The airlift continued after the war until 14 November. The United States delivered approximately 90,000 tons of materiel to Israel by sealift by the beginning of December, using 16 ships.[[361]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaberSchiff2003382-366) 33,210 tons of it arrived by November.[[365]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003276-370)

By the beginning of December, Israel had received between 34 and 40 F-4 fighter-bombers, 46 A-4 attack airplanes, 12 [C-130](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-130_Hercules "C-130 Hercules") cargo airplanes, 8 [CH-53](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CH-53_Sea_Stallion "CH-53 Sea Stallion") helicopters, 40 [unmanned aerial vehicles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle "Unmanned aerial vehicle"), 200 [M-60](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/M60_Patton "M60 Patton")/[M-48A3](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/M48_Patton "M48 Patton") tanks, 250 APCs, 226 utility vehicles, 12 [MIM-72 Chaparral](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIM-72_Chaparral "MIM-72 Chaparral") surface-to-air missile systems, three MIM-23 Hawk SAM systems, 36 155 mm artillery pieces, seven 175 mm artillery pieces, and large quantities of 105 mm, 155 mm and 175 mm ammunition. [State of the art](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_the_art "State of the art") equipment, such as the [AGM-65 Maverick](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/AGM-65_Maverick "AGM-65 Maverick") missile and the [BGM-71 TOW](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BGM-71_TOW "BGM-71 TOW"), weapons that had only entered production one or more years prior, as well as highly advanced electronic jamming equipment, was also sent. Most of the combat airplanes arrived during the war, and many were taken directly from USAF units. Most of the large equipment arrived after the ceasefire. The total cost of the equipment was approximately US$800 million (US$5.67 billion today).[[363]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003275%E2%80%93276-368)[[364]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaberSchiff2003282-369)[[366]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGawrych199656-371)[[367]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-372)

On 13 and 15 October, Egyptian air defense radar detected an aircraft at an altitude of 25,000 metres (82,000 ft) and a speed of Mach 3 (3,700 km/h; 2,300 mph), making it impossible to intercept either by fighter or SAM missiles. The aircraft proceeded to cross the whole of the canal zone, the naval ports of the Red Sea (Hurghada and Safaga), flew over the airbases and air defenses in the [Nile delta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nile_delta "Nile delta"), and finally disappeared from radar screens over the Mediterranean Sea. The speed and altitude were those of the [U.S. SR-71 Blackbird](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lockheed_SR-71_Blackbird "Lockheed SR-71 Blackbird"). According to Egyptian commanders, the intelligence provided by the reconnaissance flights helped the Israelis prepare for the Egyptian attack on 14 October and assisted it in conducting Operation Stouthearted Men.[[368]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-373)[[369]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003251%E2%80%93252-374)[[370]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-375)

### Aid to Egypt and Syria

#### Soviet supplies

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Damaged_BMP-1.jpg)

 A Syrian [BMP-1](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BMP-1 "BMP-1") captured by Israeli forces

Starting on 9 October, the Soviet Union began supplying Egypt and Syria by air and by sea. The Soviets airlifted 12,500–15,000 tons of supplies, of which 6,000 tons went to Egypt, 3,750 tons went to Syria and 575 tons went to Iraq. [General Shazly](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saad_el-Shazly "Saad el-Shazly"), the former Egyptian chief of staff, claimed that more than half of the airlifted Soviet hardware actually went to Syria. According to [Ze'ev Schiff](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ze%27ev_Schiff "Ze'ev Schiff"), Arab losses were so high and the attrition rate so great that equipment was taken directly from Soviet and Warsaw Pact stores to supply the airlift.[[371]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchiff1974303-376)[Antonov An-12](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonov_An-12 "Antonov An-12") and [An-22](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonov_An-22 "Antonov An-22") aircraft flew over 900 missions during the airlift.[[372]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003275-377)

The Soviets supplied another 63,000 tons, mainly to Syria, by means of a sealift by 30 October.[[373]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-378)[[374]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-379) Historian Gamal Hammad asserts that 400 T-55 and T-62 tanks supplied by the sealift were directed towards replacing Syrian losses, transported from [Odessa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odessa "Odessa") on the [Black Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea "Black Sea") to the Syrian port of Latakia. Hammad claimed that Egypt did not receive any tanks from the Soviets.[[375]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHammad2002382-380) The sealift may have included [Soviet nuclear weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Russia and weapons of mass destruction"), which were not unloaded but kept in Alexandria harbor until November to counter the Israeli nuclear preparations, which Soviet satellites had detected. Soviet intelligence informed Egypt that Israel had armed three nuclear weapons.[[376]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-381)

American concern over possible evidence of nuclear warheads for the Soviet Scud missiles in Egypt contributed to Washington's decision to go to [DEFCON](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/DEFCON "DEFCON") 3.[[350]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-farr-355) According to documents declassified in 2016, the move to DEFCON 3 was motivated by CIA reports indicating that the Soviet Union had sent a ship to Egypt carrying nuclear weapons along with two other amphibious vessels.[[377]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-382)

#### Soviet active aid

On the Golan front, Syrian forces received direct support from Soviet technicians and military personnel. At the start of the war, there were an estimated 2,000 Soviet personnel in Syria, of whom 1,000 were serving in Syrian air defense units. Soviet technicians repaired damaged tanks, SAMs and radar equipment, assembled fighter jets that arrived via the sealift, and drove tanks supplied by the sealift from ports to Damascus. On both the Golan and Sinai fronts, Soviet military personnel retrieved abandoned Israeli military equipment for shipment to Moscow.[[378]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004325-383)

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:T-62_tank_of_the_Syrian_Arab_Army,_1973-1974.jpg)

T-62 tank without standard Syrian camouflage, newly supplied by the Soviet Union

Soviet advisors were reportedly present in Syrian command posts "at every echelon, from battalion up, including supreme headquarters". Some Soviet military personnel went into battle with the Syrians, and it was estimated that 20 were killed in action and more were wounded. In July 1974, Israeli Defense Minister [Shimon Peres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shimon_Peres "Shimon Peres") informed the Knesset that high-ranking Soviet officers had been killed on the Syrian front during the war. There were strong rumors that a handful were taken prisoner, but this was denied. However, it was noted that certain Soviet Jews were allowed to emigrate just after the war, leading to suspicions of a covert exchange. _[The Observer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Observer "The Observer")_ wrote that seven Soviets in uniform were taken prisoner after surrendering when the Israelis overran their bunker. The Israelis reportedly took the prisoners to Ramat David Airbase for interrogation, and treated the incident with great secrecy.[[379]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-384)[[380]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-385)

Soviet fighter pilots stationed in Egypt as advisors and instructors may have participated in combat operations. There are several references to Soviet personnel being captured which were never officially confirmed, including a [US State Department](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State "United States Department of State") mention of a report from an Israeli Air Force pilot which claimed that two Soviet MiG pilots had been captured, and the account of an Israeli paratrooper reservist who claimed that while mopping up bunkers near Suez City, his force captured four or five Soviet officers. Israeli officers who reported great difficulty in command and control due to jamming of their radio frequencies attributed the improved jamming capabilities they were facing to the Soviets. According to [Gideon Remez](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gideon_Remez "Gideon Remez") and [Isabella Ginor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isabella_Ginor "Isabella Ginor"), Soviet [Spetsnaz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spetsnaz "Spetsnaz") commandos twice conducted raids behind Israeli lines on the Egyptian front in the early days of the war and captured two Israeli Centurion tanks after killing their crews so that their upgraded guns could be studied.[[381]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-386)

Israeli military intelligence reported that Soviet-piloted [MiG-25 Foxbat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-25 "Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-25") interceptor/reconnaissance aircraft overflew the Canal Zone.[[382]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-387)

#### Soviet intervention threat

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Israeli_and_Egyptian_Generals_Meet_in_Sinai_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg)

24 October. A UN-arranged meeting between IDF Lt. Gen. [Haim Bar-Lev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haim_Bar-Lev "Haim Bar-Lev") and Egyptian Brigadier General Bashir Sharif in Sinai.[[383]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyne2002p._142_Insert_6-388)

On 9 October, the Soviet cultural center in Damascus was damaged during an IAF airstrike, and two days later, the Soviet merchant ship _Ilya Mechnikov_ was sunk by the Israeli Navy during a battle off Syria. The Soviets condemned Israeli actions, and there were calls within the government for military retaliation. The Soviets ultimately reacted by deploying two destroyers off the Syrian coast. Soviet warships in the Mediterranean were authorized to open fire on Israeli combatants approaching Soviet convoys and transports. There were several recorded instances of Soviet ships exchanging fire with Israeli forces. In particular, the Soviet minesweeper _Rulevoi_ and the medium landing ship _SDK-137_, guarding Soviet transport ships at the Syrian port of Latakia, fired on approaching Israeli jets.[[384]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-littlerock-389)

During the cease-fire, Henry Kissinger mediated a series of exchanges with the Egyptians, Israelis and the Soviets. On 24 October, Sadat publicly appealed for American and Soviet contingents to oversee the ceasefire; it was quickly rejected in a White House statement. Kissinger also met with Soviet Ambassador Dobrynin to discuss convening a peace conference with Geneva as the venue. Later in the evening (9:35 pm) of 24–25 October, Brezhnev sent Nixon a "very urgent" letter.[[385]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuandt2005121-390)[[386]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004479-391)

In that letter, Brezhnev began by noting that Israel was continuing to violate the ceasefire and it posed a challenge to both the U.S. and USSR. He stressed the need to "implement" the ceasefire resolution and "invited" the U.S. to join the Soviets "to compel observance of the cease-fire without delay". He then threatened "I will say it straight that if you find it impossible to act jointly with us in this matter, we should be faced with the necessity urgently to consider taking appropriate steps [unilaterally](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unilateralism "Unilateralism"). We cannot allow arbitrariness on the part of Israel."[[387]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuandt2005121Rabinovich2004497-392)

Kissinger immediately passed the message to [White House Chief of Staff](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Chief_of_Staff "White House Chief of Staff")[Alexander Haig](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Haig "Alexander Haig"), who met with Nixon for 20 minutes around 10:30 pm, and reportedly empowered Kissinger to take any necessary action.[[385]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuandt2005121-390) Kissinger immediately called a meeting of senior officials, including Haig, Defense Secretary [James Schlesinger](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Schlesinger "James Schlesinger") and CIA Director [William Colby](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Colby "William Colby"). The [Watergate scandal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watergate_scandal "Watergate scandal") had reached its apex, and Nixon was so agitated and discomposed that they decided to handle the matter without him:

> When Kissinger asked Haig whether [Nixon] should be wakened, the White House chief of staff replied firmly 'No.' Haig clearly shared Kissinger's feelings that Nixon was in no shape to make weighty decisions.[[388]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004480-393)

The meeting produced a conciliatory response, which was sent (in Nixon's name) to Brezhnev. At the same time, it was decided to increase the DEFCON from four to three. Lastly, they approved a message to Sadat (again, in Nixon's name) asking him to drop his request for Soviet assistance, and threatening that if the Soviets were to intervene, so would the United States.[[388]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004480-393)

The Soviets placed seven airborne divisions on alert and airlift was marshaled to transport them to the Middle East. An airborne command post was set up in the southern Soviet Union, and several air force units were also alerted. "Reports also indicated that at least one of the divisions and a squadron of transport planes had been moved from the Soviet Union to an airbase in [Yugoslavia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslavia "Yugoslavia")".[[389]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-394)

The Soviets quickly detected the increased American defense condition, and were astonished and bewildered at the response. "Who could have imagined the Americans would be so easily frightened," said [Nikolai Podgorny](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Podgorny "Nikolai Podgorny"). "It is not reasonable to become engaged in a war with the United States because of Egypt and Syria," said Premier [Alexei Kosygin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexey_Kosygin "Alexey Kosygin"), while KGB chief [Yuri Andropov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Andropov "Yuri Andropov") added that "We shall not unleash the [Third World War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_III "World War III")."[[390]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004484-395) The letter from the U.S. cabinet arrived during the meeting. Brezhnev decided that the Americans were too nervous, and that the best course of action would be to wait to reply.[[391]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004485-396) The next morning, the Egyptians agreed to the American suggestion, and dropped their request for assistance from the Soviets, bringing the crisis to an end.

#### Other countries

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:JG-8_Schautafel.jpg)

A plaque commemorating the supply of eight [East German Air Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_German_Air_Force "East German Air Force") MiG-21s to Syria during the war, on display at the Flugplatzmuseum [Cottbus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cottbus "Cottbus")

In total, Arab countries added up to 100,000 troops to Egypt and Syria's frontline ranks, and about 20,000 troops stationed in Jordanian territory.[[11]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich200454-11) Besides Egypt, Syria, Jordan, and Iraq, several other Arab states were also involved in this war, providing additional weapons and financing. In addition to its forces in Syria, Iraq sent a single [Hawker Hunter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawker_Hunter "Hawker Hunter") squadron to Egypt. The squadron quickly gained a reputation amongst Egyptian field commanders for its skill in air support, particularly in anti-armor strikes.[[392]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003277%E2%80%93278-397)

However, nearly all Arab reinforcements came with no logistical plan or support, expecting their hosts to supply them, and in several cases causing logistical problems. On the Syrian front, a lack of coordination between Arab forces led to several instances of friendly fire.[[4]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-tlas-4)[[2]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003278-2)

*   [Algeria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria") sent a squadron each of MiG-21s and [Su-7s](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Su-7 "Su-7") to Egypt, which arrived at the front between 9 and 11 October. It also sent an armored brigade of 150 tanks, the advance elements of which began to arrive on 17 October, but reached the front only on 24 October, too late to participate in the fighting. After the war, during the first days of November, Algeria deposited around US$200 million with the Soviet Union to finance arms purchases for Egypt and Syria.[[2]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003278-2) Algerian fighter jets, however, did participate in attacks together with Egyptians and Iraqis.[[393]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-kuwaraswamy60-398)
*   [East German](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") Communist Party leader [Erich Honecker](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erich_Honecker "Erich Honecker") directed the shipment of 75,000 grenades, 30,000 mines, 62 tanks and 12 fighter jets to Syria.[[394]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-fisher1993-399)
*   20 [North Korean](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") pilots and 19 non-combat personnel were sent to Egypt.[[7]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly200383%E2%80%9384-7) According to Shlomo Aloni, the last aerial engagement on the Egyptian front, which took place on 6 December, saw Israeli F-4s engage North Korean-piloted MiG-21s.[[8]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-david2013-8) The Israelis shot down one MiG, and another was mistakenly shot down by Egyptian air defenses. Egyptian sources said that the North Koreans suffered no losses but claimed no aerial victories in their engagements.[[202]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolleCooper2004-206)[_[page needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_][[222]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAloni2001-226)[_[page needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_][[7]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly200383%E2%80%9384-7)
*   According to Chengappa, several [Pakistan Air Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Air_Force "Pakistan Air Force") pilots flew combat missions in Syrian aircraft, and shot down one Israeli fighter.[[395]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Chengappa2004-400)[[396]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Dunstan2003-401)[[397]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Kumaraswamy2013-402)
*   [Libya](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libya "Libya"), which had forces stationed in Egypt before the outbreak of the war, provided one armored brigade and two squadrons of [Mirage V](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirage_V "Mirage V") fighters, of which one squadron was to be piloted by the Egyptian Air Force and the other by Libyan pilots. Only Egyptian-manned squadrons participated in the war.[[393]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-kuwaraswamy60-398) The Libyan armored brigade stationed in Egypt never took an active part in the war.[[393]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-kuwaraswamy60-398) Libya also sent financial aid.[[398]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-403)
*   [Saudi Arabia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia") had a force of 20,000 Saudi soldiers that remained in Jordanian territory since 1967 to provide support and assistance as needed for a total of 10 years.[[22]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-okaz2019-23)[[21]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-sauditw-22)[[23]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-cmu1978-24) Additionally, the Saudis sent 3,000 soldiers to Syria, bolstered by a light armored battalion of [Panhard AML-90](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panhard_AML "Panhard AML") vehicles.[[3]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004464%E2%80%93465-3) One of the AMLs was later captured by the Israelis near Golan Heights and displayed to the media as proof of Saudi involvement.[[216]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Ballance1979-220)[_[page needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] The Saudi armor was deployed primarily in rearguard actions[[216]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Ballance1979-220)[_[page needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] but also performed active reconnaissance for the Iraqi and Jordanian expeditionary forces between 16 and 19 October.[[399]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Syrianfront-404) During that time, it participated in two major engagements and the IDF claimed that most of the armoured car battalion was destroyed.[[399]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Syrianfront-404) The Saudis acknowledged only minor losses, including the loss of 4 AMLs.[[216]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Ballance1979-220)[_[page needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]
*   [Kuwait](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait") dispatched 3,000 soldiers to Syria.[[3]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004464%E2%80%93465-3) These arrived with additional Jordanian and Iraqi reinforcements in time for a new Syrian offensive scheduled for 23 October, which was later cancelled.[[3]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004464%E2%80%93465-3)[Kuwaiti troops](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jahra_Force "Al Jahra Force") were also sent to Egypt.[[400]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-almasryalyoum-405)[_[better source needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")_][[401]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-406) Kuwait also provided financial aid.[[402]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004464-407)
*   [Morocco](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco") sent one infantry brigade to Egypt and one armored regiment to Syria.[[392]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003277%E2%80%93278-397)[[402]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004464-407) Six Moroccan troops were killed in action on the Syrian front.[[5]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-tobji-5)
*   [Tunisia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia") sent 1,000–2,000 soldiers to Egypt, where they were stationed in the Nile Delta and some of them were stationed to defend Port Said.[[4]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-tlas-4)
*   Lebanon enabled Palestinian artillery units to operate from its territory and Lebanese radar operators guided Syrian air force aircraft.[[403]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-408) Lebanon however did not directly take part in the war.[[404]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-409)
*   [Sudan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudan "Sudan") deployed a 3,500-strong infantry brigade to Egypt. It arrived on 28 October, too late to participate in the war.

_Non-state participants_:

*   An infantry brigade composed of [Palestinians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinians "Palestinians") was in Egypt before the outbreak of the war.[[4]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-tlas-4)[[402]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004464-407)

### Palestinian attacks from Lebanese territory

During the course of the war, Palestinian militias from southern Lebanon launched several attacks on Israeli border communities. All of the attempts to infiltrate Israel failed, and 23 militants were killed and four were captured during the clashes. Most of the activity was focused on [Katyusha rocket](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher "Katyusha rocket launcher") and anti-tank missile fire on Israeli border communities. In the attacks some civilians were injured, mostly lightly and damage was made to property. On 10 October, after Palestinian militants fired some 40 rockets on Israeli communities, Chief of Staff David Elazar and chief of the [Northern Command](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Northern_Command "Israeli Northern Command") Yitzhak Hofi requested permission to send a force into Lebanon to root out Palestinian militants, but the request was declined by Defense Minister Moshe Dayan, who did not want to divert forces from the Syrian front.[[405]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-410)[[406]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004411-411)

UN-backed ceasefire
-------------------

A 1974 news report about warfare on the Golan prior to the May disengagement accords

On 24 October, the UNSC passed [Resolution 339](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_339 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 339"), serving as a renewed call for all parties to adhere to the ceasefire terms established in Resolution 338. Most heavy fighting on the Egyptian front ended by 26 October, but clashes along the ceasefire lines and a few airstrikes on the Third Army took place. With some Israeli advances taking place, Kissinger threatened to support a UN withdrawal resolution, but before Israel could respond, Egyptian national security advisor [Hafez Ismail](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Hafez_Ismail "Mohammed Hafez Ismail") sent Kissinger a stunning message –Egypt was willing to enter into direct talks with Israel, provided that it agree to both allowing non-military supplies to reach the Third Army and to a complete ceasefire.

About noon on 25 October, Kissinger appeared before the press at the State Department. He described the various stages of the crisis and the evolution of U.S. policy. He reviewed the first two weeks of the crisis and the nuclear alert, reiterated opposition to U.S. and Soviet troops in the area and more strongly opposed unilateral Soviet moves. He then reviewed the prospects for a peace agreement, which he termed "quite promising", and had conciliatory words for Israel, Egypt and even the USSR. Kissinger concluded his remarks by spelling out the principles of a new U.S. policy toward the Arab–Israeli conflict saying:[[407]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-412)

> Our position is that ... the conditions that produced this war were clearly intolerable to the Arab nations and that in the process of negotiations it will be necessary to make substantial concessions. The problem will be to relate the Arab concern for the sovereignty over the territories to the Israeli concern for secure boundaries. We believe that the process of negotiations between the parties is an essential component of this.

Quandt considers, "It was a brilliant performance, one of his most impressive." One hour later the United Nations Security Council adopted [Resolution 340](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_340 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 340"). This time the ceasefire held, and the fourth Arab–Israeli war was over.

Disengagement
-------------

Main article: [Agreement on Disengagement between Israel and Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agreement_on_Disengagement_between_Israel_and_Syria "Agreement on Disengagement between Israel and Syria")

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:UN_Kilometer_101.jpg)

UN Emergency Forces at Kilometre 101, November 1973

Disengagement talks took place on 28 October 1973, at "Kilometre 101" between Israeli Major General [Aharon Yariv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aharon_Yariv "Aharon Yariv") and Egyptian Major General [Abdel Ghani el-Gamasy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdel_Ghani_el-Gamasy "Abdel Ghani el-Gamasy"). Ultimately, Kissinger took the proposal to Sadat, who agreed. United Nations checkpoints were brought in to replace Israeli ones, nonmilitary supplies were allowed to pass, and [prisoners-of-war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_of_war "Prisoner of war") were to be exchanged.

A [summit conference in Geneva](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva_Conference_(1973) "Geneva Conference (1973)") followed in December 1973. All parties to the war—Israel, Syria, Jordan and Egypt—were invited to a joint effort by the Soviet Union and the United States to finally usher peace between the Arabs and Israelis. This conference was recognized by UN Security Council Resolution 344 and was based on the Resolution 338, calling for a "just and durable peace". Nevertheless, the conference was forced to adjourn on 9 January 1974, as Syria refused attendance.[[408]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-413)

After the failed conference, Henry Kissinger started conducting [shuttle diplomacy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shuttle_diplomacy "Shuttle diplomacy"), meeting with Israel and the Arab states directly. The first concrete result of this was the initial military disengagement agreement, signed by Israel and Egypt on 18 January 1974. The agreement commonly known as Sinai I had the official name of _Sinai Separation of Forces Agreement_. Under its terms, Israel agreed to pull back its forces from the areas West of Suez Canal, which it had occupied since the end of hostilities. Moreover, Israeli forces were also pulled back on the length of the whole front to create security zones for Egypt, UN and Israel, each roughly ten kilometres wide. Thus Israel gave up its advances reaching beyond the Suez canal, but it still held nearly all of Sinai. It became the first of many such _Land for Peace_ agreements where Israel gave up territory in exchange for treaties.[[409]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Tristam-414)

On the Syrian front, skirmishes and artillery exchanges continued taking place. Shuttle diplomacy by Henry Kissinger eventually produced a [disengagement agreement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agreement_on_Disengagement_between_Israel_and_Syria "Agreement on Disengagement between Israel and Syria") on 31 May 1974, based on exchange of prisoners-of-war, Israeli withdrawal to the [Purple Line](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purple_Line_(border) "Purple Line (border)") and the establishment of a UN buffer zone. The agreement ended the skirmishes and exchanges of artillery fire that had occurred frequently along the Israeli-Syrian ceasefire line. The [UN Disengagement and Observer Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Disengagement_Observer_Force_Zone "United Nations Disengagement Observer Force Zone") (UNDOF) was established as a peacekeeping force in the Golan. On June 26, president Hafez al-Assad [raised the national flag](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raising_the_flag_over_Quneitra "Raising the flag over Quneitra") over the city of [Quneitra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quneitra "Quneitra").

The peace discussion at the end of the war was the first time that Arab and Israeli officials met for direct public discussions since the aftermath of the [1948 war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War "1948 Arab–Israeli War").

Reactions
---------

### Response in Israel

Though the war reinforced Israel's military deterrence, it had a stunning effect on the population in Israel. Following their victory in the Six-Day War, the Israeli military had become complacent. The shock and sudden reversals that occurred at the beginning of the war inflicted a terrible psychological blow to the Israelis, who had hitherto experienced no serious military challenges.[[410]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004497%E2%80%93498-415)

A protest against the Israeli government started four months after the war ended. It was led by [Motti Ashkenazi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motti_Ashkenazi "Motti Ashkenazi"), commander of Budapest, the northernmost of the Bar-Lev forts and the only one during the war not to be captured by the Egyptians.[[411]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004499-416) Anger against the Israeli government (and Dayan in particular) was high. [Shimon Agranat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shimon_Agranat "Shimon Agranat"), President of the [Israeli Supreme Court](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel "Supreme Court of Israel"), was asked to lead an inquiry, the Agranat Commission, into the events leading up to the war and the setbacks of the first few days.[[412]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004501-417)

[Shmuel Gonen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shmuel_Gonen "Shmuel Gonen"), commander of the Southern front, was recommended by the initial report to be relieved of active duty.[[413]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004502-418) He was forced to leave the army after the publication of the Commission's final report, on 30 January 1975, which found that "he failed to fulfill his duties adequately, and bears much of the responsibility for the dangerous situation in which our troops were caught."[[414]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-419)[_[better source needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")_]

Rather than quieting public discontent, the report—which "had stressed that it was judging the ministers' responsibility for security failings, not their parliamentary responsibility, which fell outside its mandate"—inflamed it. Although it had absolved Meir and Dayan of all responsibility, public calls for their resignations (especially Dayan's) intensified.[[413]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004502-418)

On 11 April 1974, Golda Meir resigned. Her cabinet followed suit, including Dayan, who had previously offered to resign twice and was turned down both times by Meir. A new government was seated in June and Yitzhak Rabin, who had spent most of the war as an advisor to Elazar in an unofficial capacity, became prime minister.[[415]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004237-420)

### Response in Egypt

General Shazly had angered Sadat for advocating the withdrawal of Egyptian forces from Sinai to meet the Israeli incursion on the West Bank of the Canal. Six weeks after the war, he was relieved of command and forced out of the army, ultimately going into political exile for years. Upon his return to Egypt, he was placed under house arrest.[[416]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004507-421)

Following his release, he advocated the formation of a "Supreme High Committee" modeled after Israel's Agranat Commission in order to "probe, examine and analyze" the performance of Egyptian forces and the command decisions made during the war, but his requests were completely ignored.[[417]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003331-422) He published a book, banned in Egypt, that described Egypt's military failings and the sharp disagreements he had with Ismail and Sadat in connection with the prosecution of the war.[[418]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShazly2003334-423)

The commanders of the Second and Third Armies, Generals Khalil and Wasel, were also dismissed from the army.[[416]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004507-421) The commander of the Egyptian Second Army at the start of the war, General Mamoun, suffered a heart attack,[_[citation needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] or, alternatively, a breakdown, after the Egyptian defeat during the 14 October Sinai tank battle, and was replaced by General Khalil.[[419]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004356-424)[[420]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-425)

### Response in Syria

In Syria, Colonel Rafik Halawi, the [Druze](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druze "Druze") commander of an infantry brigade that had collapsed during the Israeli breakthrough, was executed before the war even ended.[_[dubious](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy\_dispute#Disputed\_statement "Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute") – [discuss](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Yom\_Kippur\_War#Dubious "Talk:Yom Kippur War")_][[416]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004507-421) He was given a quick hearing and sentenced to death;[_[dubious](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy\_dispute#Disputed\_statement "Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute") – [discuss](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Yom\_Kippur\_War#Dubious "Talk:Yom Kippur War")_] his execution was immediate.[_[dubious](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy\_dispute#Disputed\_statement "Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute") – [discuss](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Yom\_Kippur\_War#Dubious "Talk:Yom Kippur War")_][[421]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Eartkquake-426) Military historian [Zeev Schiff](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeev_Schiff "Zeev Schiff") referred to him as Syria's "sacrificial lamb".[[421]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Eartkquake-426) The Syrians however offered vehement denials that Halawi was executed and expended great efforts trying to debunk the allegation.[[422]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Halawi-427) They claimed he was killed in battle with Israel and threatened severe punishment to anyone repeating the allegation of execution.[[422]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Halawi-427)

Their concern stemmed from a desire to maintain Syrian Druze loyalty to Assad's regime and prevent Syrian Druze from siding with their co-religionists in Israel.[[422]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Halawi-427) On 7 July 1974, Halawi's remains were removed from a Syrian military hospital and he was interred in Damascus at the "Cemetery of the Martyrs of the October War" in the presence of many Syrian dignitaries.[[422]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Halawi-427) One analyst noted that the presence of so many high-level officials was unusual and attributed it to Syrian efforts to quell any suggestion of execution.[[422]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Halawi-427)

### Response in the Soviet Union

According to [Anatoly Chernyaev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatoly_Chernyaev "Anatoly Chernyaev"), on 4 November 1973, Soviet leader [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev") said:

> We have offered them (the Arabs) a sensible way for so many years. But no, they wanted to fight. Fine! We gave them technology, the latest, the kind even Vietnam didn't have. They had double superiority in tanks and aircraft, triple in artillery, and in air defense and anti-tank weapons they had absolute supremacy. And what? Once again they were beaten. Once again they scrammed [_[sic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sic "Sic")_]. Once again they screamed for us to come save them. Sadat woke me up in the middle of the night twice over the phone, "Save me!" He demanded to send Soviet troops, and immediately! No! We are not going to fight for them.[[423]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Chernyaev1973p69-428)

### Arab oil embargo

In response to U.S. support of Israel, the Arab members of OPEC, led by [King Faisal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_of_Saudi_Arabia "Faisal of Saudi Arabia") of [Saudi Arabia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia"), decided to reduce oil production by 5% per month on 17 October. On 19 October, President Nixon authorized a major allocation of arms supplies and $2.2 billion in appropriations for Israel. In response, Saudi Arabia declared an embargo against the United States, later joined by other oil exporters and extended against the Netherlands and other countries, causing the [1973 energy crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_oil_crisis "1973 oil crisis").[[424]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-429)

Aftermath
---------

Analyses differ on the military outcome of the war; as an Israeli victory by some military historians,[[438]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-443) and by others, as a military stalemate.[[448]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-453)

### Egyptian–Israeli disengagement agreement

Main article: [Sinai Interim Agreement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Interim_Agreement "Sinai Interim Agreement")

Another Egyptian–Israeli disengagement agreement, the _Sinai Interim Agreement_, was signed in Geneva on 4 September 1975, and was commonly known as Sinai II. This agreement led Israel to withdraw from another 20–40 km with UN forces buffering the vacated area. After the agreement, Israel still held more than two-thirds of Sinai, which would prove to be a valuable bargaining chip in the coming negotiations.[[449]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-454)

### Egyptian–Israeli Camp David Accords

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sadat_and_Begin_clean3.jpg)

Egyptian President Anwar Sadat and Israeli Prime Minister [Menachem Begin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menachem_Begin "Menachem Begin") acknowledge applause during a joint session of Congress in Washington, D.C., during which President [Jimmy Carter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter "Jimmy Carter") announced the results of the [Camp David Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_David_Accords "Camp David Accords"), 18 September 1978.

Main article: [Camp David Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_David_Accords "Camp David Accords")

The Yom Kippur War upset the status quo in the Middle East, and the war served as a direct antecedent of the 1978 Camp David Accords.[[210]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-The_1973_Arab-Israeli_War-214) The impetus for the talks came when United States President [Jimmy Carter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter "Jimmy Carter") invited both Sadat and Begin to a summit at [Camp David](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_David "Camp David") to negotiate a final peace. The talks took place from 5–17 September 1978. Ultimately, the talks succeeded, and Israel and Egypt signed the Egypt–Israel Peace Treaty in 1979. Israel subsequently withdrew its troops and settlers from the Sinai, in exchange for normal relations with Egypt and a lasting peace, with the last Israeli troops exiting on 26 April 1982.[[450]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-455)

The Accords resulted in the [Egypt–Israel peace treaty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty"), the first ever between Israel and an Arab state. According to [George Friedman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Friedman "George Friedman"), the war gave the Israelis increased respect for the Egyptian military and decreased their confidence in their own, and caused the Israelis to be uncertain whether they could defeat Egypt in the event of another war. At the same time, the Egyptians recognized that despite their improvements, the Israelis survived in the end, and became doubtful that they could ever defeat Israel militarily. Therefore, a negotiated settlement made sense to both sides.[[451]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-456) Many in the [Arab world](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world") were outraged at Egypt's peace with Israel. Sadat, in particular, became deeply unpopular both in the Arab world and in his own country. Egypt was suspended from the Arab League until 1989. Until then, Egypt had been "at the helm of the Arab world".[[452]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-457)

### U.S. military doctrine

See also: [AirLand Battle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/AirLand_Battle "AirLand Battle")

U.S. military studies of the Yom Kippur War played a major role in shaping U.S. [military doctrine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_doctrine "Military doctrine") in subsequent decades,[[453]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-458)[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459) particularly because the U.S. Army's [Training and Doctrine Command (TRADOC)](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army_Training_and_Doctrine_Command "United States Army Training and Doctrine Command") was established only three months before the onset of the war. U.S. Army Chief of Staff Gen. [Creighton Abrams](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creighton_Abrams "Creighton Abrams"), TRADOC Commander Gen. [William E. DePuy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_E._DePuy "William E. DePuy"), and other Army leaders saw Israel's strategic and doctrinal conditions between 1967 and 1973 as similar to NATO's position in Europe, and thus they undertook a deep study of Israel's warfighting in 1973 to derive insights for war against the Soviet Union.[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459)

Soon after the war, U.S. Army civilian analysts and senior officers such as Gen. [Donn A. Starry](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donn_A._Starry "Donn A. Starry") visited the IDF and compiled "lessons" for the Army to learn after the war.[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459) These lessons covered the improved lethality and accuracy of anti-tank and anti-air missiles, the importance of superior training for tank crews, the necessity of cover and concealment during movement, and the importance of [combined arms](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combined_arms "Combined arms") warfare.[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459) In 1976, TRADOC revised the Army's FM 100–5 _Operations_ field manual and promoted an operational concept of "Active Defense", with a strong emphasis on tactical proficiency tied to the performance of advanced weapons systems like those observed in the Yom Kippur War fighting.[[455]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Romjue-460) Gen. DePuy visited Israel in 1976, where he toured Yom Kippur War battlefields and observed Israeli field training. He used these insights to encourage reforms of U.S. Army training to ease the Army's transition to a more professional force after the end of the military draft in 1973.[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459)

In May 1977, Gen. Starry (soon to succeed DePuy as TRADOC commander) returned to Israel and toured Yom Kippur War sites on the Golan Heights, guided by [Raful Eitan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raful_Eitan "Raful Eitan") and [Moshe Peled](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moshe_Peled_(politician) "Moshe Peled (politician)").[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459) Starry used his observations to address problems left unaddressed by the Active Defense doctrine, such as how best to fight follow-on echelons after the first battle. TRADOC's 1982 revision of FM 100–5 replaced Active Defense with an offense-oriented operational doctrine known as [AirLand Battle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/AirLand_Battle "AirLand Battle"), which formed the basis of the American plan for [Operation Desert Storm](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Desert_Storm "Operation Desert Storm") in 1991.[[454]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Bronfeld-459)[[455]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Romjue-460)

Casualties
----------

See also: [Israeli casualties of war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_casualties_of_war "Israeli casualties of war")

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Downed_Mirage.jpg)

A downed Israeli Mirage

Israel suffered between 2,521[[426]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated450-431)[[39]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchiff1974328-40)[[30]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated87-31) and 2,800 killed in action.[[29]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGawrych2000243-30) An additional 7,250[[34]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004497-35) to 8,800[[29]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGawrych2000243-30) soldiers were wounded. Some 293 Israelis were captured.[[31]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated2004-32) Approximately 400 Israeli tanks were destroyed. Another 600 were disabled but returned to service after repairs.[[41]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004496-42) A major Israeli advantage, noted by many observers, was their ability to quickly return damaged tanks to combat.[[456]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Gal-461)

The Israeli Air Force lost 102 airplanes: 32 F-4s, 53 A-4s, 11 Mirages and 6 Super Mysteres. Two helicopters, a Bell 205 and a CH-53, were lost.[[42]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-White_House_Military_Briefing-43) According to Defense Minister Moshe Dayan, nearly half of these were shot down during the first three days of the war.[[37]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Herzog,_260-38)[_[full citation needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#What\_information\_to\_include "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] IAF losses per combat sortie were less than in the Six-Day War of 1967.[[457]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-462)

Arab casualties were known to be much higher than Israel's. Precise figures are difficult to ascertain as Egypt and Syria never disclosed official figures. The lowest casualty estimate is 8,000 (5,000 Egyptian and 3,000 Syrian) killed and 18,000 wounded.[[29]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGawrych2000243-30) The highest estimate is 18,500 (15,000 Egyptian and 3,500 Syrian) killed.[[30]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated87-31) Most estimates lie somewhere in between the two, with the Insight Team of London's _[The Sunday Times](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Sunday\_Times "The Sunday Times")_ putting combined Egyptian and Syrian losses at 16,000 killed.[[426]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated450-431) Another source cites a figure of some 15,000 dead and 35,000 wounded.[[35]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004496%E2%80%93497-36) U.S. estimates placed Egyptian casualties at 13,000.[[458]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-463) Iraq lost 278 killed and 898 wounded, while Jordan suffered 23 killed and 77 wounded.[[32]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Dunstan,_p._200-33) Morocco lost 170 killed.[[459]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Yabiladi-464) Some 8,372 Egyptians, 392 Syrians, 13 Iraqis and 6 Moroccans were taken prisoner.[[31]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated2004-32)[[460]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-465)

Arab tank losses amounted to 2,250[[35]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004496%E2%80%93497-36)[[461]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-466) though Gawrych cites a figure of 2,300.[[36]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGawrych2000244-37) 400 of these fell into Israeli hands in good working order and were incorporated into Israeli service.[[35]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabinovich2004496%E2%80%93497-36) Between 341[[29]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGawrych2000243-30) and 514[[37]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Herzog,_260-38) Arab aircraft were shot down. According to Herzog, 334 of these aircraft were shot down by the IAF in air-to-air combat for the loss of only five Israeli planes.[[37]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-Herzog,_260-38) The _Sunday Times_ Insight Team notes Arab aircraft losses of 450.[[426]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-autogenerated450-431) Nineteen Arab naval vessels, including 10 missile boats, were sunk for no Israeli losses.[[38]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerzog1975269-39)

Atrocities
----------

### Syrian atrocities

Syria ignored the [Geneva Conventions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva_Conventions "Geneva Conventions") and many Israeli prisoners of war were tortured or killed.[[462]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-467) Advancing Israeli forces, re-capturing land taken by the Syrians early in the war, came across the bodies of 28 Israeli soldiers who had been blindfolded with their hands bound and summarily executed.[[463]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-468) In a December 1973 address to the National Assembly, Syrian Defense Minister [Mustafa Tlass](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Tlass "Mustafa Tlass") stated that he had awarded one soldier the Medal of the Republic for killing 28 Israeli prisoners with an axe, decapitating three of them and eating the flesh of one of his victims.[[464]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-469)[[465]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-470)

The Syrians employed brutal interrogation techniques utilizing electric shocks to the genitals. A number of Israeli soldiers taken prisoner on Mount Hermon were executed. Near the village of Hushniye, the Syrians captured 11 administrative personnel from the Golan Heights Force, all of whom were later found dead, blindfolded, and with their hands tied behind their backs. Within Hushniye, seven Israeli prisoners were found dead, and another three were executed at Tel Zohar. Syrian prisoners who fell into Israeli captivity confirmed that their comrades killed IDF prisoners.[[466]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchiff201390-471)

A soldier from the Moroccan contingent fighting with Syrian forces was found to be carrying a sack filled with the body parts of Israeli soldiers which he intended to take home as souvenirs. The bodies of Israeli prisoners who were killed were stripped of their uniforms and found clad only in their underpants, and Syrian soldiers removed their [dog tags](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dog_tag "Dog tag") to make identification of the bodies more difficult.[[467]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-472)

Some Israeli POWs reported having their fingernails ripped out while others were described as being turned into human ashtrays as their Syrian guards burned them with lit cigarettes.[[468]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-arnold-473) A report submitted by the chief medical officer of the Israeli army notes that, "the vast majority of (Israeli) prisoners were exposed during their imprisonment to severe physical and mental torture. The usual methods of torture were beatings aimed at various parts of the body, electric shocks, wounds deliberately inflicted on the ears, burns on the legs, suspension in painful positions and other methods."[[469]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War#cite_note-474)
